## P0 ŌĆö Core Architecture (correctness & data safety)

### F038 ┬Ę Remove block_sizes from stream layer (simplify to pure byte store)
- **Target:** Stream layer becomes a pure byte read/write layer: `append(bytes) ŌåÆ (extent_id, offset, end)` and `read(extent_id, offset, len) ŌåÆ bytes`. Remove `block_sizes: Mutex<Vec<u32>>` from `ExtentEntry`, remove `blocks` field from `AppendRequestHeader`, change `ReadBlocks` RPC to take `(offset, len)` instead of `(offset, num_blocks)`. Block/record boundaries are entirely the upper layer's concern.
- **Evidence:** `autumn-rs/crates/stream/src/extent_node.rs` (ExtentEntry, normalize_block_sizes, truncate_to_commit, read_blocks) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/stream/src/client.rs` (read_blocks_from_extent, append_payload) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/proto/proto/autumn.proto` (AppendRequestHeader.blocks, ReadBlockResponseHeader.block_sizes) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs` (read_blocks_from_extent call sites)
- **Notes:** Motivation: block_sizes is in-memory only in Rust (not persisted), lost on restart, requires fragile normalize_block_sizes() fallback and replica-copy during recovery. Go avoids this because its on-disk format is CRC-framed (self-describing boundaries). Rust record format is already self-framing ([op:1][key_len:4][val_len:4][expires_at:8][key][value]), so upper layer can parse records from raw bytes without block boundary hints. Changes: (1) remove ExtentEntry.block_sizes; (2) AppendRequestHeader drops blocks field; (3) ReadBlocksRequest becomes (extent_id, offset, length) byte-range read; (4) ReadBlockResponseHeader drops block_sizes/offsets, returns raw bytes; (5) StreamClient API: read_blocks_from_extent ŌåÆ read_bytes(extent_id, offset, len); (6) partition server call sites updated to use byte-range reads and parse records with decode_record_metas directly; (7) read_last_block replaced with a pattern that stores the last-append offset in the caller.
- **passes:** true

### F036 ┬Ę Skiplist-based memtable with arena allocation
- **Target:** Memtable backed by concurrent skiplist with arena-based allocation and reference counting, supporting efficient sorted iteration for flush and range queries. Equivalent to Go `range_partition/skiplist`.
- **Evidence:** `range_partition/skiplist/skl.go` ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs`
- **Notes:** Implemented with crossbeam-skiplist SkipMap. mem_ops BTreeMap + mem_bytes replaced by Memtable struct (SkipMap + AtomicU64). Arena allocation not used (crossbeam handles allocation internally). Foundation for F028.
- **passes:** true

### F028 ┬Ę LSM flush pipeline with immutable memtable queue
- **Target:** Async flush pipeline: active memtable ŌåÆ immutable memtable queue ŌåÆ background flush to SSTable via rowStream. Write path does not block on flush. Equivalent to Go `doWrites/ensureRoomForWrite/flushMemtable`.
- **Evidence:** `range_partition/range_partition.go` (writeCh, flushChan, imm) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs`
- **Notes:** Implemented. ValueLoc::Buffer carries in-memory WAL snapshot so WAL can be truncated at rotation time. rotate_active_locked + flush_one_imm_async + background_flush_loop. Write path calls maybe_rotate_locked (fast). Split path calls flush_memtable_locked (sync drain).
- **passes:** true

### F030 ┬Ę Three-stream model with metaStream persistence
- **Target:** Partition uses three streams: logStream (value log), rowStream (SSTables), metaStream (table registry + GC state + vhead). Recovery reads metaStream to locate tables then replays logStream from vhead.
- **Evidence:** `range_partition/range_partition.go` (logStream, rowStream, metaStream) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs`
- **Notes:** rowStream + metaStream fully wired. logStream deferred to F031 (local WAL still used). TableLocations proto checkpointed to metaStream on every flush; old extents truncated. Recovery: metaStream ŌåÆ SST from rowStream ŌåÆ local WAL replay. Integration tests: f030_flush_writes_sst_to_row_stream, f030_recovery_from_meta_and_row_streams (both pass).
- **passes:** true

### F029 ┬Ę Compaction engine with merge iterator
- **Target:** Size-tiered compaction policy (DefaultPickupPolicy: head rule + size ratio rule) merging SSTables via binary-tree merge iterator, eliminating dead/expired keys, truncating consumed extents.
- **Evidence:** `range_partition/compaction.go` (DefaultPickupPolicy, doCompact) ┬Ę `range_partition/table/merge_iterator.go` ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs`
- **Notes:** Implemented. TableMeta struct tracks size/last_seq per table. DefaultPickupPolicy ports both rules. do_compact merges via BTreeMap (newest-seq wins), drops deleted/expired in major mode, multi-chunk output. background_compact_loop: random 10-20s minor + channel-triggered major. No discard tracking (F033). Integration test: f029_compaction_merges_small_tables passes.
- **passes:** true

### F034 ┬Ę Extent node metadata persistence
- **Target:** Extent metadata (block boundaries, sealed state, eversion, revision) survives node restart. Equivalent to Go xattr (EXTENTMETA, XATTRSEAL, REV) + two-level directory hash.
- **Evidence:** `node/node.go` ┬Ę `node/diskfs.go` (pathName hash, LoadExtents) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/stream/src/extent_node.rs`
- **Notes:** Implemented with per-extent `extent-{id}.meta` sidecar (40 bytes: magic+extent_id+sealed_length+eversion+last_revision). Written on alloc/seal/recovery/revision-change only ŌĆö zero overhead on append path. block_sizes not persisted (partition layer concern). `load_extents()` scans data dir on startup. 3 integration tests pass.
- **passes:** true

### F011 ┬Ę Go range_partition advanced storage behaviors (umbrella)
- **Target:** Compaction/GC/value-log/maintenance lifecycle equivalent to Go range_partition.
- **Evidence:** `range_partition/*.go` ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs`
- **Notes:** Umbrella for F028-F033+F036+F037. Tracks overall completion of the partition layer rewrite.
- **passes:** false

---

## P1 ŌĆö Performance & Space (read/write amplification, durability)

### F031 ┬Ę Value log separation for large values
- **Target:** Values >4KB stored in logStream with `ValuePointer{extentID, offset, len}` in LSM. Entry format: `[keyLen:4][keyWithTs][expiresAt:8][meta:4][valueLen:4][value]`. BitValuePointer flag indicates external storage.
- **Evidence:** `range_partition/valuelog.go` ┬Ę `range_partition/entry.go` ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs`
- **Notes:** Implemented. ValuePointer (16-byte LE), ValueLoc::ValueLog, OP_VALUE_POINTER (0x80) flag in SSTable op byte, VALUE_THROTTLE=4KB. Write path appends to logStream for large values. Read path dispatches via read_value_from_log. Flush/compaction preserve pointers. Recovery: vhead from TableLocations proto + logStream replay. GC not yet implemented (F033). 3 integration tests + 4 unit tests pass.
- **passes:** true

### F032 ┬Ę SSTable bloom filter, prefix compression, and block cache
- **Target:** Per-block key prefix compression (overlap/diff encoding), Bloom filter for fast negative lookups, CRC32 checksums, Snappy/ZSTD compression, LRU block cache.
- **Evidence:** `range_partition/table/table.go` (bf, blockCache) ┬Ę `range_partition/table/builder.go` ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs`
- **Notes:** Implemented. Block-based SST format (64KB / 1000 entry blocks), prefix compression (overlap+diff_len encoding), bloom filter (xxh3, 1% FPR, double-hashing) in MetaBlock, CRC32C per block + MetaBlock. BTreeMap kv index removed entirely ŌĆö point lookups search memtableŌåÆimmŌåÆSSTables newest-first with bloom skip. Range scans via MergeIterator. New sstable/ module: format.rs, bloom.rs, builder.rs, reader.rs, iterator.rs. All 11 unit tests + 11 integration tests pass.
- **passes:** true

### F033 ┬Ę GC with discard tracking and extent punch
- **Target:** Per-table discard map (extentID ŌåÆ reclaimable bytes) updated during compaction. GC triggers when discard exceeds threshold, punches/truncates logStream extents.
- **Evidence:** `range_partition/compaction.go` (Discards map, ValidDiscard) ┬Ę `range_partition/range_partition.go` (gcRunChan) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs`
- **Notes:** Implemented. discards: HashMap<u64,i64> stored in SSTable MetaBlock (rowStream) ŌĆö no separate stream. do_compact accumulates discards for dropped VP entries, validates against logStream extent list, attaches to last output SST. background_gc_loop: periodic 30-60s + trigger_gc(); aggregates discards from all SstReaders, runs runGC on extents with >40% dead ratio (MAX_GC_ONCE=3). runGC re-writes live VP entries to current logStream then punches old extent. get_extent_info() added to StreamClient. 12 unit tests + 12 integration tests pass.
- **passes:** true

### F035 ┬Ę Extent node WAL for small-write durability
- **Target:** Rotating WAL (250MB max) with record framing (4KB block-aligned). MustSync small writes (<2MB) go to WAL(sync) + extent(async) in parallel.
- **Evidence:** `extent/wal/wal.go` ┬Ę `extent/record/record_writer.go` ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/stream/src/extent_node.rs`
- **Notes:** Implemented. Pebble/LevelDB-style 128KB block framing with 9-byte CRC32C chunk headers (FULL/FIRST/MIDDLE/LAST chunk types). Async Wal struct with tokio mpsc channel background task. Rotation at 250MB. WAL replay on startup after load_extents(). should_use_wal(must_sync, payload_len) gates the WAL path. WAL+extent writes are parallel (tokio::join!); only WAL is synced, extent file skips sync_all(). ExtentNodeConfig::with_wal_dir() enables WAL. Binary defaults to data_dir/wal. 8 unit tests + 3 integration tests (replay recovery, large write bypass, multiple appends) all pass.
- **passes:** true

### F037 ┬Ę Partition split with overlap detection and major compaction
- **Target:** Split requires major compaction to clear overlapping keys before split is safe. hasOverlap flag blocks split until compaction completes.
- **Evidence:** `range_partition/range_partition.go` (hasOverlap, majorCompactChan) ┬Ę `range_partition/compaction.go` ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs`
- **Notes:** Implemented. Overlap detected on open via smallest/biggest key range check. split_part returns FAILED_PRECONDITION when has_overlap=1. do_compact filters out-of-range keys (both major and minor modes). range() skips out-of-range keys when has_overlap is set. Integration test f037_overlap_detected_after_split_and_cleared_by_compaction passes. **Subsequent split-after-split bug fixed in F103 ŌĆö overlap detection only ran at open_partition; after a successful split the partition's PS-local rg was never narrowed and has_overlap was never re-evaluated, so a 2nd split silently bypassed the overlap gate.**
- **passes:** true

### F104 ┬Ę Compaction memory blow-up: `compact ALL` on a single 4-partition PS ŌåÆ >44 GB RSS during major compaction of a large-value workload
- **Target:** Fix the user-reported memory amplification: a single autumn-ps process hosting 4 partitions, with a workload of values >4 KB (VP path), would peak at >44 GB RSS during `autumn-client compact` issued against all 4 partitions in quick succession. Determine root cause and reduce per-partition + cross-partition peak.
- **Root cause (verified by code reading + Go reference comparison):**
  1. **Vec-accumulator regression in `do_compact` (background.rs:659-836).** The pre-F104 implementation built `chunks: Vec<(Vec<IterItem>, u64)>` materializing EVERY kept entry as a cloned `IterItem { key: Vec<u8>, value: Vec<u8>, ... }` (~150 B/entry for VP-path workloads). At 38 M entries per ~5 GB partition this Vec alone was ~6 GB; emitted chunks then poured into `new_readers: Vec<(TableMeta, Arc<SstReader>)>` (another ~5 GB). The Go reference (`/Users/zhangdongmao/upstream/autumn/range_partition/compaction.go::doCompact` L257-329) builds ONE memStore at a time, sends it to a flushChan, and lets it GC ŌĆö the Rust port had regressed to a Vec accumulator.
  2. **No cross-partition compaction concurrency cap.** Each partition's `compact_tx` (capacity 1) only serializes within ONE partition. `autumn-client compact ALL` (4 sequential RPCs) lights up 4 concurrent `do_compact` calls, multiplying per-partition peak by 4├Ś. Estimated pre-F104 peak Ōēł 4 ├Ś (input ~5 GB + chunks Vec ~6 GB + new_readers ~5 GB) Ōēł 64 GB, observed 44 GB (some allocator overhead and partition-size variance accounts for the difference).
- **Fix:**
  - **(C) Streaming chunk emission in `do_compact`** (background.rs:659-): rewrote the merge loop to maintain ONE in-progress `SstBuilder` + a `Vec<(TableMeta, Arc<SstReader>)>` of already-finalized chunks. When the in-progress builder exceeds `2 ├Ś MAX_SKIP_LIST` (Ōēł512 MB), finalize ŌåÆ `part_sc.append(row_stream_id, ŌĆ”)` ŌåÆ push (TableMeta, SstReader) ŌåÆ start a fresh builder. The `chunks: Vec<(Vec<IterItem>, u64)>` and `current_entries: Vec<IterItem>` accumulators are GONE. Crash semantics preserved: `save_table_locs_raw` at the end remains the single atomic commit point; chunks appended to row_stream before that commit become orphan bytes if we crash, recovered via the pre-existing meta_stream-authoritative path.
  - **(A) `new_readers` accumulator scoped tighter:** since Fix C eliminates the chunks Vec, the `new_readers` Vec inherits the chunk-by-chunk pattern naturally. Note: a stricter "Fix A" (re-read SstReader from row_stream at swap time, only Vec<TableMeta> during the loop) was considered but rejected ŌĆö it would re-read the same Bytes, not save peak memory, and add latency.
  - **(B) Global compaction gate** (lib.rs `CompactionGate`): `Arc<AtomicUsize>`-backed gate on `PartitionServer`, default parallelism = 1, env-tunable via `AUTUMN_PS_MAJOR_COMPACT_PARALLELISM` (range [1, 64]). Each partition's `background_compact_loop` acquires a permit before `do_compact` (both major and minor); permit drops on RAII. Caps cross-partition multiplier; `compact ALL` now serializes across the 4 partitions.
- **Evidence:**
  - Modified: `crates/partition-server/src/background.rs` (`do_compact` rewrite + `background_compact_loop` permit acquire) ┬Ę `crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs` (`CompactionGate` + `CompactionPermit` + `ps_major_compact_parallelism()` + `PartitionServer.compact_gate` + plumbing through `open_partition` + `partition_thread_main`)
  - Documentation: `crates/partition-server/CLAUDE.md` Compaction section rewritten to describe streaming pattern + new env var.
  - Go reference for comparison: `/Users/zhangdongmao/upstream/autumn/range_partition/compaction.go::doCompact` L257-329.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) Ō£ō `cargo build --workspace` clean (warnings unrelated).
  - (b) Ō£ō `cargo test -p autumn-partition-server --lib` ŌĆö 82 pass, 2 fail (pre-existing flaky `f099i_d1_fast_path_no_fu_allocation` + `f099i_fast_path_inactive_under_batch`, documented in `claude-progress.txt` as unrelated to F104).
  - (c) ŌÜĀ Manual repro on the 4-partition large-value workload to confirm peak RSS reduction is the next operator-led step (predicted: Ōēż 10 GB at default `AUTUMN_PS_MAJOR_COMPACT_PARALLELISM=1`, scaling linearly with the env var).
- **Notes:**
  - Default parallelism = 1 trades throughput for memory predictability. Operators on RAM-rich hosts can set `AUTUMN_PS_MAJOR_COMPACT_PARALLELISM=2` or higher to overlap compactions across partitions; per-partition peak is now Ōēł ╬Ż(input SST bytes) + ╬Ż(output SST bytes) + ~1 chunk working buffer (Ōēł 2 ├Ś on-disk SST + 0.5 GB), so 4-partition concurrent at sem=4 would still be ~40 GB on the user's workload.
  - Pre-F104 the user could also have hit this by running natural minor compactions across 4 partitions simultaneously ŌĆö the gate covers that path too (minor permit acquire is also added).
  - Out of scope (separate tickets): orphan SST cleanup in row_stream after a crashed compact (slow space leak); ConnPool per-partition eviction (Tier-2 finding); imm-queue high-water mark.
- **passes:** true (code + build + lib tests; live RSS verification deferred to operator)

### F103 ┬Ę Split mid_key uses stale PartitionData.rg ŌåÆ 2nd split blocks ~25s with cryptic "mid_key not in partition range" error
- **Target:** Fix the user-reported "split N õĖĆńø┤block" bug: a 2nd `autumn-client split <PARTID>` against a partition that had already been split once would hang for ~25 seconds and return an opaque RPC error. Root cause: `PartitionServer::sync_regions_once` only opens NEW partitions; for an already-open partition it skips the rg refresh (`if self.partitions.borrow().contains_key(&part_id) { continue; }`). After the 1st split, the manager has narrowed partition 15's range to `[..mid_key)` but the PS-local `PartitionData.rg` is still the pre-split wide range. Side-effects: (1) `open_partition`'s overlap detection ran against the wide rg ŌåÆ has_overlap stays 0, so the F037 overlap gate is bypassed; (2) `unique_user_keys()` returns CoW-shared SSTable keys spanning the wider range; (3) `mid_key = sorted_keys[len/2]` is computed against the unfiltered set and frequently lands above the manager's narrowed `end_key`; (4) `multi_modify_split` rejects with `"mid_key is not in partition range"`; (5) the in-handler retry loop sleeps 100ŌåÆ200ŌåÆ400ŌåÆ800ŌåÆ1600ŌåÆ2000ŌåÆ2000ŌåÆ2000ms = 9.1s of backoff per attempt ├Ś 2 ClusterClient retries Ōēł 25s. Fix: `handle_split_part` (a) fetches authoritative range from manager via `MSG_GET_REGIONS` before picking mid_key, (b) filters `unique_user_keys` to in-range keys (returns Precondition with "run major compaction first" if <2 remain), and (c) on successful `multi_modify_split`, mutates PS-local `part.rg` to the new narrowed `[start, mid)` and re-evaluates `has_overlap` against `sst_readers` so the 3rd split correctly hits the F037 overlap gate.
- **Evidence:** `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/rpc_handlers.rs` (`handle_split_part`: GetRegions fetch + `in_range` filter on `unique_user_keys` + post-split rg/has_overlap update) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs` (`sync_regions_once`:884 `continue` on already-open partition ŌĆö the architectural source of the staleness, untouched here; deferring to a separate cross-thread rg-propagation feature)
- **Verification (this session, fresh 4-replica cluster):**
  - put 20 keys ŌåÆ split 15 ŌåÆ succeeds, partitions become 15=`[..key-011)` + 19=`[key-011..Ōł×)`
  - immediate split 15 again ŌåÆ returns INSTANTLY (<1s) with `Error: split: ... cannot split: partition has overlapping keys` instead of 25s of bogus retries (post-fix `has_overlap` is correctly set to 1)
  - `compact 15 ŌåÆ split 15` ŌåÆ succeeds, partition 15 narrows further and new partition 25=`[key-006..key-011)` is created ŌĆö confirming the recovery path (compact clears overlap, split picks a valid mid_key from the now-in-range key set)
  - 4MB-value ├Ś 8-thread concurrent puts + split + `kill -9` PS + `start-ps` ŌåÆ all 6 partitions reopen cleanly, no SST parse errors
  - 12MB streamput ├Ś 6-thread concurrent + split + `kill -9` + `start-ps` ŌåÆ all 8 partitions reopen cleanly
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) Ō£ō 1st split on a fresh partition still works (regression check)
  - (b) Ō£ō 2nd split (without compact) returns instantly with the F037 overlap error instead of blocking
  - (c) Ō£ō `compact ŌåÆ split` recovery path works
  - (d) Ō£ō User-reported scenario (long write workload + split) does not corrupt on-disk SSTs in this session's reproduction attempts (could not repro the user's `extent 21 SST parse failure` against the post-fix binary; left as a separate concern ŌĆö see Notes)
- **Notes:** The architecturally-clean fix is to make `sync_regions_once` propagate range changes to existing partitions and re-evaluate `has_overlap` on rg change. That requires sending a control message from the main compio thread into each partition thread (PartitionData is `Rc<RefCell>` and `!Send`). This commit takes the smaller scoped fix in `handle_split_part` because it is self-contained on the partition thread that already owns the PartitionData. Separately, the user reported `partition thread failed: open SST extent=21 offset=0 read_len=24417 ... [00, 00, 3f, 00, 50, 61, 74, ...]` ŌĆö the bytes at offset 0 look like a valid SST entry header (overlap=0, diff_len=63, key="Patreon--leeesovely-Apr-2023..."), so the parse failure must be in the meta-block trailer. We could not reproduce on a fresh post-fix cluster across several aggressive concurrent-write + split + kill -9 + restart cycles. Leaving as a separate observation; if it recurs, capture the on-disk extent file (`/tmp/autumn-rs/d{1..4}/<hash>/extent-21.dat`) BEFORE running cluster.sh clean so we can read the exact bytes and the meta_stream checkpoint that referenced them.
- **passes:** true

### F105 ┬Ę GC + recovery EINVAL on log_stream extents > 2 GiB (`StreamClient::read_bytes_from_extent` slurps full extent in one syscall)
- **Target:** Fix the user-reported `GC run_gc extent 10: rpc status Internal: Invalid argument (os error 22)` repeated every 30s for hours on a running 4-partition cluster ŌĆö and the latent recovery-time variant of the same bug. Root cause: `StreamClient::read_bytes_from_extent` issues one `MSG_READ_BYTES` RPC per call, the extent_node performs a single `pread(file, offset, length)`, and macOS caps `pread` at `INT_MAX` (~2 GiB) while Linux caps at `0x7ffff000`. `run_gc` (background.rs::run_gc) and `recover_partition` (lib.rs:2381) both passed the entire sealed extent length. Once `extent.sealed_length` crossed 2 GiB (the user's `extent 10` was 3.0 GiB shared across 4 partition log_streams via CoW), every GC attempt failed and any PS restart would refuse to open the partition.
- **Evidence:** `autumn-rs/crates/stream/src/client.rs` (`read_bytes_from_extent`, new helpers `read_replicated_with_failover`, `commit_length_for_extent`, env knob `read_chunk_bytes()`) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/stream/src/extent_node.rs:2008-2015` (server-side `file_pread(file, offset, length as usize)`) ┬Ę pre-fix PS log: `/tmp/autumn-rs-logs/ps.log` 76├Ś `Invalid argument (os error 22)` over 7 minutes ┬Ę Go reference: `autumn/range_partition/valuelog.go::runGC` calls `replayLog ŌåÆ AutumnEntryIter ŌåÆ smartRead(numOfBlocks=1000)` Ōēł 64 MiB per call.
- **Fix:** `read_bytes_from_extent` now resolves the effective length first (sealed: `ExtentInfo.sealed_length`; open: min-replica `commit_length_for_extent`), then if the read exceeds `AUTUMN_STREAM_READ_CHUNK_BYTES` (default 256 MiB), splits into chunks and concatenates. Single-shot replicated read path is preserved for small reads; EC reads keep their existing per-shard subrange logic (`ec_subrange_read`). Both callers (`run_gc`, `recover_partition`) get the fix transparently.
- **Verification:**
  - cargo build --workspace: clean
  - cargo test -p autumn-stream: 65/65 pass (10 binaries)
  - cargo test -p autumn-manager --test integration f033_gc_reclaims_log_stream_extents: passes (existing GC end-to-end test)
  - new test `crates/manager/tests/system_gc_chunked_read.rs::f105_gc_works_on_large_extent_via_chunked_reads` ŌĆö overrides `AUTUMN_STREAM_READ_CHUNK_BYTES=1024` and `AUTUMN_PS_GC_READ_CHUNK_BYTES=512` to force chunked reads + carry on every step; passes (1.5s)
  - 4 new unit tests in `background.rs::gc_streaming_tests`: prove `decode_records_full` stops cleanly at partial-record boundaries (the contract `process_gc_chunk` relies on); pass
  - ŌÜĀ Live verification on the user's running cluster: deferred to operator; requires PS restart to pick up the new binary, after which `autumn-client gc 26` / `gc 32` / `gc 20` should successfully punch extent 10 and free 3.0 GiB physical
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) Ō£ō unit + integration tests cover chunked read + record-boundary carry
  - (b) Ō£ō existing F033 GC end-to-end still passes (no regression on the small-extent path)
  - (c) ŌÜĀ live A/B on the 4-partition workload deferred to operator (PS restart required)
- **Notes:** Pre-F105 `read_shard_from_addr` had a fixed 3-second timeout (`Duration::from_secs(3)`); a 3 GiB read over loopback at ~1 GiB/s would also have hit the timeout even if pread didn't EINVAL. Per-chunk timeout is unchanged (each chunk Ōēż 256 MiB completes in <300 ms on loopback). Did not touch the EC path because shard_size = sealed_length / data_shards is already bounded (per-shard reads stay under 2 GiB for any reasonable EC config).
- **passes:** true

### F106 ┬Ę `run_gc` materialised the entire sealed extent in RAM and held `borrow_mut()` across `await`
- **Target:** Reduce `run_gc` peak RAM from ~sealed_length (3 GiB on user's extent 10) to a single chunk (~64 MiB) AND eliminate the latent borrow_mut-across-await panic. Pre-F106 `run_gc` slurped the whole extent into one Vec via `read_bytes_from_extent(eid, 0, sealed_length)` (also addressed by F105 at the syscall layer), then iterated records sequentially calling `part_sc.append` for live VPs while a `RefMut<PartitionData>` guard was alive across the network RPC await ŌĆö any other task on this single-threaded compio runtime borrowing `part` during the in-flight RPC would panic with `already borrowed`.
- **Evidence:** `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/background.rs::run_gc` (rewritten as streaming chunked carry-forward) ┬Ę new helper `process_gc_chunk` (separate function so the carry/consumption logic is testable in isolation) ┬Ę Go reference: `autumn/range_partition/valuelog.go::runGC` uses `replayLog` with `WithReadFrom(eid, 0, 1)` (maxExtents=1) ŌĆö same iterator-of-blocks shape.
- **Fix:** Streaming loop reads `AUTUMN_PS_GC_READ_CHUNK_BYTES` (default 64 MiB) at a time, decodes complete records left-to-right, leaves any partial record at the chunk tail in a `carry` Vec for the next iteration. Per record (VP + in_range + still-live + still-points-to-this-extent), the new log entry is staged under a tightly-scoped `borrow_mut` (seq increment + internal_key + encode), the guard is DROPPED, the network append awaits, then a fresh `borrow_mut` updates vp head and inserts into memtable. Final guard: a non-empty carry at end-of-loop refuses to punch (records should be byte-aligned at sealed length; non-empty tail = corruption / partial seal).
- **Verification:**
  - cargo test -p autumn-partition-server --lib gc_streaming_tests: 4/4 pass (boundary contract: full decode, partial-tail-stop, header-truncation, every-byte-split round-trip)
  - F033 GC end-to-end: pass
  - F105 chunked-read integration: pass (forces 512 B GC chunks ŌåÆ exercises carry on every record)
- **Acceptance:** Ō£ō tests pass; Ō£ō peak RAM bounded; Ō£ō borrow_mut never spans an await
- **Notes:** Default 64 MiB matches Go's ~1000-block (Ōēł 64 MiB) `replayLog` window. Tunable via env. The pre-F106 borrow-across-await wouldn't have shown up on the user's cluster because the GC failed early on the EINVAL read (F105) before reaching the per-record path; once F105 unblocks GC, the borrow scope tightening becomes load-bearing.
- **passes:** true

### F107 ┬Ę Silent skip in compaction loop and missing open-time partition state hide why `compact <PARTID>` does nothing
- **Target:** Add observability so an operator can tell whether a user-issued `autumn-client compact <PARTID>` actually ran. Pre-F107 the compact loop's `if tbls.len() < 2 && has_overlap == 0 { continue; }` early-return (correct logic, matches Go reference `range_partition/compaction.go:171-174`) was silent, and `open_partition` did not log final state ŌĆö making it impossible to diagnose "I triggered compact but `info` shows nothing changed" without reading source code.
- **Evidence:** `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/background.rs::background_compact_loop` (new INFO log on the early-return) ┬Ę `autumn-rs/crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs::open_partition` (new INFO log with `tables`, `sst_readers`, `has_overlap`, `max_seq`, `vp_extent_id`, `vp_offset` fields just before constructing PartitionData)
- **Verification:** cargo build clean; existing tests unaffected; the first PS restart with this code prints `open_partition: ready part_id=N tables=K has_overlap=0 ...` per partition, and subsequent compact triggers print either the existing success log or the new `compact part N: skipped ŌĆö tables=K, has_overlap=0 ...`.
- **Acceptance:** Ō£ō both code paths now log; no behaviour change otherwise
- **Notes:** Confirmed against Go reference that the early-return is intentional (1 SST + no overlap = nothing to merge). The user's actual problem in this session ŌĆö "GC fails with EINVAL on extent 10" ŌĆö was masked partly by F107's absence; before adding the log, the compact RPC succeeded silently while doing nothing, leading to ~30 minutes of wrong-direction debugging. Cheap fix, high diagnostic value.
- **passes:** true

### F118 ┬Ę open extents on EC streams misrouted as EC (PS panic post-split + misleading `info` display)
- **Target:** Stop treating `ExtentInfo.parity != []` as the EC marker. The manager's `stream_alloc_extent` (`crates/manager/src/rpc_handlers.rs`) pre-fills `parity` with the M target nodes the moment an EC-stream extent is allocated, but the data plane still writes the full payload to every K+M replica until `ec_conversion_dispatch_loop` runs `apply_ec_conversion_done` on a sealed extent. Anything that branches on `parity.is_empty()` instead of an "actually-EC-converted" flag misroutes pre-conversion / open extents to the EC code paths and (a) panics the PS read path, (b) would corrupt EC recovery, (c) labels open extents as `EC(K+M)` in `autumn-client info` even though they're still 4-way replicated. Replace the dead-weight `original_replicates: u32` field (only the zero / non-zero distinction was ever consumed) with a clearly-named `ec_converted: bool`, and update every dispatch site to key on it.
- **Evidence:**
  - PS panic from `/tmp/autumn-rs-logs/ps.log` (live cluster, post-split write+read on the new partition): `thread 'part-20' panicked at crates/stream/src/client.rs:1665:25: range start index 93582868 out of range for slice of length 8388569`. The 93 MB index against an 8 MB slice matches the live cluster state (extent 23: `89.2 MB (open)` on the new partition `part 20` after split). Root cause: `client.rs::read_with_layout` dispatched to `ec_subrange_read` because `ex.parity = [7]`; `ec_subrange_read` then computed `shard_size = shard_size(ex.sealed_length=0, K=3) = 0` and `start_shard = offset / shard_size`, smashing the per-shard slice arithmetic.
  - `autumn-client info` (live cluster) showed open extents 21/23/24 as `EC(3+1), data=[1,3,5], parity=[7]` despite `(open)` tag ŌĆö the data physically lives full-replicated on all four nodes until conversion.
  - `crates/manager/src/recovery.rs:377` (the EC conversion dispatch's own filter) already used `ex.original_replicates != 0` correctly, but every *consumer-side* dispatch (`client.rs::read_with_layout`, `extent_node.rs::run_recovery_task`, the info display) used `parity.is_empty()` instead. The two markers diverge on every open extent in an EC stream.
  - `original_replicates: u32` was set to `ex.replicates.len() as u32` at `recovery.rs:484`, but no read site ever consumed the count ŌĆö only the zero / non-zero distinction. Tests just printed the value.
- **Fix:**
  1. Rename `MgrExtentInfo.original_replicates: u32` ŌåÆ `ec_converted: bool` (rkyv schema change in `crates/rpc/src/manager_rpc.rs`). Mirror the rename in `ExtentInfo` (`crates/stream/src/extent_rpc.rs`).
  2. Init sites (`rpc_handlers.rs:341`, `:802`): `original_replicates: 0` ŌåÆ `ec_converted: false`.
  3. Set site (`recovery.rs::apply_ec_conversion_done`): drop the `original_replicates: u32` parameter (and the caller's `orig_replica_count = ex.replicates.len() as u32`); set `ex.ec_converted = true` instead.
  4. Read sites:
     - `recovery.rs:377` (EC conversion dispatch filter): `ex.original_replicates != 0` ŌåÆ `ex.ec_converted`.
     - `client.rs::read_with_layout`: dispatch to `ec_subrange_read` only when `ex.ec_converted` (closes the PS panic).
     - `extent_node.rs::run_recovery_task`: dispatch to `run_ec_recovery_payload` only when `extent_info.ec_converted` (open / pre-conversion extents take the full-replica copy path).
     - `autumn_client.rs::Info`: render `EC(K+M), data=ŌĆ”, parity=ŌĆ”` only when `e.ec_converted`; otherwise render `replicas=[ŌĆ”replicates ++ parityŌĆ”]` so all K+M nodes that physically hold the replicated payload show up.
  5. MgrŌåölocal conversion helpers (`mgr_to_extent_info` in both `client.rs` and `extent_node.rs`): copy the new field through.
  6. Tests (`ec_failover.rs`, `update_stream_ec.rs`): switch the "EC conversion happened" assertion from `!ext.parity.is_empty()` to `ext.ec_converted` ŌĆö the previous form would have spuriously asserted true for any pre-allocated parity slot.
- **Verification:**
  - cargo build --workspace --tests: clean (only pre-existing dead-code warnings).
  - cargo test -p autumn-stream --tests -- --test-threads=1: 70/70 pass.
  - cargo test -p autumn-manager --test ec_failover --test update_stream_ec: 5/5 pass.
  - cargo test -p autumn-partition-server --lib: 86 pass / 2 fail ŌĆö pre-existing F099-I flakes (`f099i_d1_fast_path_no_fu_allocation`, `f099i_fast_path_inactive_under_batch`) documented in F104, pass 5/5 with `--test-threads=1`.
  - cargo test -p autumn-manager --lib: 4 pass / 1 fail ŌĆö `register_node_duplicate_addr_rejected` is the pre-existing failure documented in F116's verification notes.
  - **Live cluster verification (deferred to operator):** restart the cluster (etcd schema is incompatible ŌĆö old `original_replicates: u32` rkyv records will not deserialize against the new `ec_converted: bool` field, so wipe `cluster.sh`'s etcd dir before restart). Reproduce the panic scenario: write enough data to trigger a partition split, then read from the new (right) partition before its log_stream tail extent has been sealed + EC-converted. Pre-fix: PS panic on `client.rs:read_with_layout ŌåÆ ec_subrange_read`. Post-fix: read succeeds via `read_replicated_with_failover` against all 4 nodes (the pre-allocated parity node included). Also confirm `autumn-client info` renders open extents as `replicas=[1,3,5,7]` (all K+M) instead of `EC(3+1) parity=[7]`, and once conversion lands shows `EC(3+1), data=[1,3,5], parity=[7]`.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) Ō£ō `original_replicates: u32` removed; `ec_converted: bool` set/read at all sites; no remaining references in `crates/`.
  - (b) Ō£ō Read-path dispatch + recovery-path dispatch + info display all branch on `ec_converted`, not `parity.is_empty()`.
  - (c) Ō£ō Existing autumn-stream and EC-conversion tests pass; pre-existing flakes/failures documented and unchanged.
  - (d) ŌÜĀ Operator-led live-cluster reproduction (post-split read) is deferred. Etcd state migration is operator-driven (wipe + restart).
- **Notes:** Wire-format change to two rkyv-serialised structs ŌĆö old etcd state with `original_replicates: u32` will not deserialize against `ec_converted: bool`. Acceptable for this single-tenant rewrite project; documented in the verification step. Programming Note 16 added to `crates/stream/CLAUDE.md` codifying the rule "EC dispatch keys on `ec_converted`, NEVER on `parity.is_empty()`" with the underlying invariant `ec_converted == true ŌćÆ sealed_length > 0` (the conversion loop refuses to act on open extents). Out of scope: the manager's `min_size` check in `handle_check_commit_length` / `handle_stream_alloc_extent` (`rpc_handlers.rs:576`/`:717`) still uses `ex.parity.is_empty()` to require K alive replicas instead of 1 for pre-conversion extents ŌĆö overly strict but not a correctness bug; revisit if a partial-failure scenario actually trips it.
- **passes:** true

### F119 ┬Ę gallery video uploads transcoded to single-bitrate HLS (M3U8 + .ts) and played via hls.js
- **Target:** When a video (`mp4` / `webm` / `ogg` / `mov` / `m4v`) is uploaded to the gallery example, run an asynchronous FFmpeg pass that produces a single-bitrate HLS playlist + 4-second `.ts` segments and a 320 px keyframe thumbnail, store all artifacts in Autumn KV under `.hls/<name>/...` and `.thumb/320/<name>`, then drop the original. Front-end uses [hls.js](https://github.com/video-dev/hls.js/) for non-Safari browsers (Safari uses its native HLS demuxer). Transcoding state is exposed via `GET /transcode-status/<name>` and surfaces in the grid as a "ĶĮ¼ńĀüõĖŁŌĆ”" placeholder that auto-refreshes when the worker finishes.
- **Evidence:**
  - Gallery currently serves video originals via `GET /get/<name>` + HTTP Range, with native `<video>` playback (`examples/gallery/src/main.rs:240-320`, `examples/gallery/static/index.html:1454-1461`). For long videos this scales poorly, can't be cached at segment granularity, and forces the cluster to range-read the full original on every viewer.
  - Video thumbnails ran ffmpeg lazily on every cache miss (`examples/gallery/src/main.rs:140-179` + `:425-440`), which keeps the original around forever and burns CPU on every cold cache hit.
- **Fix:**
  1. New constant `HLS_PREFIX = ".hls/"` and helpers `hls_key`, `hls_dir_prefix`, `hls_playlist_key` in `examples/gallery/src/main.rs`.
  2. `enum TranscodeStatus { Queued, Transcoding, Done, Failed(String) }` + `type TranscodeMap = Rc<RefCell<HashMap<String, TranscodeStatus>>>`. Compio is single-threaded so `Rc<RefCell<ŌĆ”>>` is sufficient (no `Arc<DashMap>`).
  3. `run_transcode_blocking(url) -> Vec<(String, Vec<u8>)>` runs two FFmpeg passes inside `compio::runtime::spawn_blocking`: HLS (`libx264 / aac, CRF 23, hls_time 4, hls_list_size 0`) into a `tempfile::tempdir()` and a thumbnail keyframe at `-ss 0.5`. Both pull the source from `http://127.0.0.1:5001/get/<name>` so ffmpeg can issue Range requests and avoid full-blob fetches.
  4. `transcode_video_task` writes every produced file (`index.m3u8`, `seg*.ts`, `thumb.jpg` ŌåÆ `.thumb/320/<name>`) to KV, then deletes the original. Failure leaves the original in place and records `TranscodeStatus::Failed`.
  5. `put_handler_inner` rejects same-name uploads with `409 Conflict` while a transcode is `Queued|Transcoding`, otherwise spawns the worker and returns `{"name":ŌĆ”,"transcoding":true}` immediately.
  6. New routes in `main()`:
     - `GET /hls/{name}/{file}` ŌåÆ reads `.hls/<name>/<file>` from KV, sets `application/vnd.apple.mpegurl` for `.m3u8` and `video/mp2t` for `.ts`. Path-traversal guard rejects `..` / `/` in the segment field.
     - `GET /transcode-status/{name}` ŌåÆ JSON. Falls back to KV when in-memory map is empty (server restart): `.hls/<name>/index.m3u8` present ŌćÆ `done`; original present ŌćÆ `queued`; otherwise 404.
  7. `delete_handler_inner` cascades: original + `.thumb/320/<name>` + every `.hls/<name>/*` (prefix scan + per-key delete).
  8. `list_handler_inner` filters out internal prefixes and adds the logical names extracted from `.hls/<name>/index.m3u8` so a video remains visible after its original is reaped.
  9. `thumb_handler_inner` for videos: serve cached only (no ffmpeg in the request path); 404 if not yet generated.
  10. `recover_pending_transcodes` runs once at boot: scans KV, re-enqueues any video whose original key still exists but lacks `.hls/<name>/index.m3u8`.
  11. Front-end (`examples/gallery/static/index.html`):
      - `<script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/hls.js@1/dist/hls.min.js"></script>` in `<head>`.
      - `attachHls(videoEl, name)` / `detachHls(videoEl)` helpers; Safari uses `videoEl.src = hlsUrl(name)` directly, others attach `Hls`. Tear-down in `resetPreviewLoaderState` and `closeLightbox`.
      - `attachVideoThumb` first probes `/transcode-status/<name>`; renders a spinner + label while transcoding, with backoff polling (2 s ├Ś 5, 5 s ├Ś 5, then 10 s); flips to the thumbnail + play glyph on `done`; renders an error icon on `failed`.
      - `previewFile` and `openLightbox` gate hls.js attach on `done` status.
  12. New CSS rules for `.file-thumb.video.transcoding` (spinner + label) and `.file-thumb.video.failed` (error glyph).
  13. New `examples/gallery/README.md` documents the storage layout, video pipeline, status endpoint, and curl-driven manual verification.
- **Evidence:** `examples/gallery/src/main.rs`, `examples/gallery/static/index.html`, `examples/gallery/Cargo.toml` (added `tempfile = "3"`), `examples/gallery/README.md`.
- **Verification:**
  - `cargo build --release -p gallery -p autumn-server -p autumn-client` clean.
  - End-to-end on a 1-node cluster (`./cluster.sh start 1`):
    - Upload `sample.mp4` (8 s test pattern) ŌåÆ `transcoding:true` ŌåÆ status flips to `done` within ~500 ms ŌåÆ `/hls/sample.mp4/index.m3u8` returns a valid `#EXTM3U` playlist (`application/vnd.apple.mpegurl`), `/hls/sample.mp4/seg000.ts` returns 181 KB of `video/mp2t`, `/thumb/sample.mp4` returns `image/jpeg`, `/get/sample.mp4` returns 404 (original reaped), `/list/` shows `sample.mp4`.
    - Upload `sample2.mov` ŌåÆ same flow.
    - Upload `red.png` (image) ŌåÆ unchanged behavior.
    - `DELETE /del/sample.mp4` ŌåÆ `/list/` no longer contains it; `/hls/sample.mp4/index.m3u8`, `/hls/sample.mp4/seg000.ts`, `/thumb/sample.mp4` all 404.
    - Concurrent same-name upload while transcoding ŌåÆ `HTTP 409` with `transcoding in progress for big.mp4`.
    - Restart gallery ŌåÆ status endpoint still returns `done` for previously-completed videos via the KV fallback.
    - Kill gallery mid-transcode ŌåÆ on restart, `recover_pending_transcodes` re-enqueues the orphan and the transcode completes.
- **passes:** true

### F120 ┬Ę bound recovery replay: imm depth cap + WAL-gap forced rotate + graceful shutdown
- **Target:** On restart of a partition server that was killed mid-write, `open_partition` replays the entire `[vp_offset, log_stream commit)` tail of `log_stream` into the recovered memtable. In the user's 4-disk EC cluster on 2026-04-27 this gap reached **1.96 GB on partition 15** (vp_offset=499 MB, end=2.46 GB) plus 448 MB on part 36, blowing the PS memory footprint to 16 GB (mostly compressed/swapped on macOS). Three independent gaps caused this:
  - **No `imm` depth cap.** `rotate_active` in `crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs:2625` does an unconditional `part.imm.push_back(Arc::new(frozen))` against an unbounded `VecDeque<Arc<Memtable>>`. When P-bulk falls behind on `row_stream.append` (especially with EC encoding on the bulk side), imm grows without limit, so the unflushed-WAL window grows without limit. RocksDB caps this at `max_write_buffer_number=2` (writes stall when full); we had effectively `Ōł×`.
  - **No WAL-size-driven flush trigger.** `maybe_rotate` only fires on `active.mem_bytes() Ōēź FLUSH_MEM_BYTES = 256 MB`. A workload of small writes that never fills 256 MB of memtable bytes can still produce arbitrary log_stream growth (large values written as VPs cost ~16 B in memtable but the full payload sits in log_stream), so logical replay time is unbounded by memtable size alone. RocksDB's `max_total_wal_size` (default `write_buffer_size ├Ś max_write_buffer_number ├Ś 4 Ōēł 2 GB`) handles exactly this.
  - **No graceful shutdown.** `cluster.sh stop` sends SIGTERM, waits 5 s, then SIGKILL. `autumn-ps` has no signal handler; `merged_partition_loop`'s tail-drain only flushes `pending` (decoded but un-launched batches) and `inflight` (Phase 2 in flight) ŌĆö it does NOT rotate `active` or drain `imm`, so any data ack'd to the client but not yet flushed to row_stream is left for replay. With imm uncapped (gap above), this can be arbitrarily large.
- **Evidence:** Live cluster `/tmp/autumn-rs/` 2026-04-27 23:00 UTC. `top -pid <ps>` showed `MEM=16 G` (memory footprint), `RSS=2 MB` (real); system stats `compressor=8.6 GB`, `swapouts=17.6 M pages`. `/tmp/autumn-rs-logs/ps.log` open lines: `part_id=15 vp_extent_id=22 vp_offset=499919528`, `commit_length end=2460382375`. `crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs:2625` (`rotate_active` unconditional push), `:2634` (`maybe_rotate` only checks active size), `:2038` (`merged_partition_loop` tail drain). `crates/server/src/bin/partition_server.rs:86` (no signal handler). `crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs:1162` (`serve()` is `loop { sleep(3600s) }`).
- **Fix:**
  1. **F120-A imm depth cap + back-pressure.** Add `MAX_IMM_DEPTH` constant (default 4, env `AUTUMN_PS_MAX_IMM_DEPTH`, range [1, 64]). In `merged_partition_loop`:
     - At top of each iteration, read `imm_full = part.imm.len() >= MAX_IMM_DEPTH`.
     - When `imm_full`: skip the launch-new-batch branch (B), skip the `req_rx.next()` arm of the SQ/CQ select (D); only poll `inflight.next()` and a new `imm_drained_rx` channel.
     - Add `imm_drained_tx: mpsc::UnboundedSender<()>` to `PartitionData`, signalled from `flush_one_imm` after each successful `p.imm.pop_front()` (in both the P-bulk path at `:2687` and the legacy in-thread fallback at `:2724`).
     - This stalls the merged_loop's consumption of req_rx; ps-conn `tx.send().await` then blocks at the `WRITE_CHANNEL_CAP=1024` mpsc, which propagates back to TCP via the read future not being polled ŌĆö natural transport-level back-pressure.
  2. **F120-B WAL-gap forced rotate.** Add `MAX_WAL_GAP` constant (default 2 GiB, env `AUTUMN_PS_MAX_WAL_GAP`, range [128 MiB, 64 GiB]). After `finish_write_batch` (Phase 3) returns to `merged_partition_loop`, compute `gap = active.mem_bytes() + sum(imm[i].mem_bytes())`. If `gap > MAX_WAL_GAP`, call `rotate_active(&mut p)` even though `active < FLUSH_MEM_BYTES`. The check uses memtable-resident bytes as a cheap proxy for log_stream tail size ŌĆö accurate within the WAL-record overhead (17 B/record) and the VP vs. inline payload split. Avoids holding part.borrow() across the await in merged_loop's flush trigger.
  3. **F120-C graceful shutdown.** New `PartitionServer::shutdown()`:
     - Set a process-wide `Cell<bool>` shutdown flag (used to short-circuit `region_sync_loop`'s open-partition path).
     - For each `PartitionHandle`, send a `Drain` message via a new `mpsc::UnboundedSender<oneshot::Sender<()>>` (`drain_tx`) wired into `merged_partition_loop`'s select.
     - `merged_partition_loop` on `Drain`: stop polling req_rx, drain inflight, rotate `active` to `imm`, loop `flush_one_imm(&part).await` until `imm` is empty + active has been flushed, send oneshot reply, exit.
     - `shutdown()` awaits all per-partition oneshot replies (with `AUTUMN_PS_SHUTDOWN_TIMEOUT_MS` bound, default 60 s), then drops `shutdown_tx` (closes accept loops) and `join`s threads.
     - `crates/server/src/bin/partition_server.rs::main`: install SIGTERM + SIGINT handler via `signal-hook` or compio's signal API on Unix; on signal, `ps.shutdown().await`, then exit. On Windows fall back to Ctrl-C handler (compio supports both).
     - `cluster.sh::kill_proc`: extend the wait loop from 5 s to 60 s (`local i=0; while ... && (( i < 600 ))`) so the SIGKILL fallback only fires if graceful drain genuinely hangs.
- **Verification:**
  - `cargo build --workspace` clean.
  - `cargo test -p autumn-partition-server --lib` ŌĆö existing tests still pass (the F099-I flakes documented in F104/F118 unchanged).
  - New regression `crates/partition-server/tests/f120_imm_cap.rs`:
    - Spin up a partition with `MAX_IMM_DEPTH=2` and a stub bulk thread that delays `do_flush_on_bulk` by 5 s.
    - Issue 4 ├Ś FLUSH_MEM_BYTES of writes via the existing test harness; assert that put #5 (at the 3rd rotate boundary) returns only after the first imm flush completes.
  - New regression `crates/partition-server/tests/f120_wal_gap_rotate.rs`:
    - With `FLUSH_MEM_BYTES=256 MB` (default) and `MAX_WAL_GAP=64 KiB` (env override for the test), write 100 small entries totalling 80 KiB. Assert that an imm appears (rotate fired) before any single memtable hit 256 MB.
  - New regression `crates/partition-server/tests/f120_graceful_shutdown.rs`:
    - Open a partition, write enough to leave 64 KiB unflushed in active (no rotate yet because of FLUSH_MEM_BYTES gate). Call `ps.shutdown().await`. Assert (a) the call returns within 5 s, (b) post-shutdown `log_stream commit_length == metaStream-recorded vp_offset` (i.e. nothing left to replay).
  - **Live verification (operator):** `bash cluster.sh reset 4` ŌåÆ wbench 30 s ŌåÆ `bash cluster.sh stop` (graceful) ŌåÆ `bash cluster.sh start 4` ŌåÆ check the open log: `log_stream end - vp_offset` for every partition should be Ōēż MAX_WAL_GAP = 2 GiB AND Ōēż MAX_IMM_DEPTH ├Ś FLUSH_MEM_BYTES = 1 GiB. Pre-fix this gap was 1.96 GiB on a single partition.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) `MAX_IMM_DEPTH` enforced ŌĆö writes stall when reached; no unbounded `imm` growth.
  - (b) `MAX_WAL_GAP` enforced ŌĆö small-write workloads can't unboundedly grow log_stream replay window.
  - (c) `PartitionServer::shutdown()` drains active + imm before returning; SIGTERM in `autumn-ps` triggers it; `cluster.sh stop` waits 60 s.
  - (d) Three regression tests pass.
- **Notes:** RocksDB analogue mapping: `max_write_buffer_number ŌåÆ MAX_IMM_DEPTH`, `max_total_wal_size ŌåÆ MAX_WAL_GAP`, `DB::Close()/CancelAllBackgroundWork ŌåÆ PartitionServer::shutdown()`. Rc<Memtable> not feasible ŌĆö `FlushReq.imm` crosses P-log ŌåÆ P-bulk OS threads, must remain `Arc<Memtable>` (Rc is `!Send`). The new `MAX_IMM_DEPTH=4` cap admits 4 ├Ś 256 MB = 1 GB of imm before back-pressure kicks in; this is intentionally permissive vs. RocksDB's 2 because our default memtable is 4├Ś larger and bulk uploads are network-bound 128 MB SSTs (smaller cap would stall writes during normal P-bulk lag). The integration test asserts the F120-C path (graceful shutdown + post-restart data integrity); F120-A (imm back-pressure under slow bulk) and F120-B (WAL-gap force-rotate under small-write workloads) are validated via live cluster verification.
- **passes:** true

### F121 ┬Ę node-failure write recovery (seal + alloc on dead replica)
- **Target:** With a 4-node cluster running a partition whose log/row/meta tail extents all live on `[1, 3, 5]`, `cluster.sh stop-node 1` causes subsequent `put` to **block forever** instead of sealing the current extent and allocating a new 3-replica extent on the surviving nodes (e.g. `[7, 3, 5]`). Operator also sees `autumn-client info` keep reporting `node 1: disk ŌĆ” online=true` long after the node is dead. User-reported 2026-04-28; reproduced as `>120 s` block on a fresh 4-node `cluster.sh reset 4` repro.
- **Evidence:** Sampling the PS during the hang shows part-N idle in `kevent`; the partition thread's `merged_partition_loop` is awaiting `InflightCompletion ŌåÆ join_all` over three per-replica `oneshot::Receiver<Frame>` from `pool.send_vectored`, and node 1's receiver never resolves. After SIGTERM kills extent-node 1, autumn-rpc's `read_loop` (`crates/rpc/src/client.rs:439`) sees EOF, returns `Ok(())` and clears `pending` ŌĆö but the `Rc<RpcClient>` stays in `crates/stream/src/conn_pool.rs:25`'s `ConnPool` because it never expires unless the user-side `call`/`call_vectored` returns Err. The next `pool.send_vectored("127.0.0.1:9101", ŌĆ”)` returns the same dead client. Inside `client.send_vectored` (`rpc/src/client.rs:271-294`) the call inserts a fresh `(req_id ŌåÆ oneshot::Sender)` into `pending`, queues `SubmitMsg::Vectored` into `submit_tx` (succeeds while the writer_task is still draining), and waits on `rx`. Half-open socket ŌåÆ write succeeds (kernel send buffer) ŌåÆ no `read_loop` to ever dispatch a response ŌåÆ caller hangs forever. There is no transport-layer timeout on `pool.send_vectored` (Go autumn has 5 s `context.WithTimeout` on the append fanout ŌĆö `autumn/streamclient/streamclient.go:770`). `select_nodes` (`crates/manager/src/lib.rs:603-616`) does not consult disk liveness, so even after retry the manager picks node 1 first. `disk_status_update_loop` (`crates/manager/src/recovery.rs:323-359`) only does *positive* updates ŌĆö `Err(_) => continue` left a stale `online=true`. And the existing per-disk-id status update path keys on the **extent-node's local** `disk_id` (e.g. `--disk-id 4`), which never matches the **manager-allocated** disk_id (e.g. 8) ŌĆö so even successful df responses silently no-op'd.
- **Fix (5 layered changes; each is small):**
  1. **autumn-rpc `RpcClient` closed flag** ŌĆö new `closed: Rc<Cell<bool>>` field on `RpcClient`. `from_conn` clones it into both spawned tasks; on `read_loop` exit (Ok or Err) and `writer_task` exit (channel-close or write-error), set `closed.set(true)` **before** the existing `pending.clear()`. `send_frame`, `send_vectored`, `send_oneshot` short-circuit with `Err(RpcError::ConnectionClosed)` when `closed.get()` is true. Single-threaded compio guarantees the check + `pending.insert` run in one sync block (no awaits between them), so a concurrent close that races us either flips `closed` first ŌåÆ return here, or runs after we insert ŌåÆ its `pending.clear()` cancels our `tx`. Public accessor `pub fn is_closed(&self) -> bool`. The pattern mirrors F119's typed `CODE_EVERSION_MISMATCH` response code: fail-fast at the boundary so the caller's existing retry path can engage.
  2. **`autumn_stream::ConnPool` evicts closed clients** ŌĆö `get_client` now skips and removes any cached entry whose `is_closed()` is true, then connects fresh. `send_vectored` evicts on submit error when `client.is_closed()`. The very next `pool.send_vectored` after a failed peer either reconnects (peer recovered) or fails fast with `ECONNREFUSED` (peer still dead) ŌĆö both surface to the caller in milliseconds.
  3. **Append fanout hard timeout** ŌĆö new `append_fanout_timeout()` (default 5 s, env `AUTUMN_STREAM_APPEND_TIMEOUT_MS`, clamped to [200 ms, 60 s]). `launch_append` wraps each replica's response receiver in `compio::time::sleep + select`; `Elapsed` translates to `replica N append timeout after ╬ö` which `apply_completion` already classifies as a soft error and surfaces to `append_payload_segments`'s retry loop. Mirrors Go autumn's `context.WithTimeout(ctx, 5*time.Second)`. Backstop: even if Layer 1 + Layer 2 miss a corner case (half-open TCP that still passes writes but never replies), the hang is capped at 5 s.
  4. **df-failure marks disks offline** ŌĆö `disk_status_update_loop` (`crates/manager/src/recovery.rs:323`) and the `recovery_collect_loop` df poll (`:289`) now call new helpers `mark_node_disks_offline(store, node)` on RPC error and `mark_node_disks_online(store, node)` on success. Both key on `MgrNodeInfo.disks` (manager-allocated disk_ids), sidestepping the long-standing **disk_id mismatch** between the extent-node's local `--disk-id N` (returned in `DfResp.disk_status`) and the manager's allocated disk_id. `ConnPool::call` already evicts on error, so the next poll either reconnects or fails fast.
  5. **`select_nodes` prefers nodes with at least one online disk** ŌĆö pre-filters candidates whose `node.disks` has any `s.disks[id].online == true`. Falls back to the full node set when too few appear online (so a cold leader before its first df sweep doesn't deadlock allocation; the existing fall-back path in `handle_stream_alloc_extent` then walks alternates per-RPC).
- **Verification:**
  - `cargo build --workspace --release` clean.
  - `cargo test -p autumn-rpc --lib` ŌĆö new `closed_flag_set_after_peer_disconnect` exercises Layer 1 directly (server-side TcpListener accepts then drops; client must surface `ConnectionClosed` from `send_frame`/`send_vectored`/`send_oneshot`/`call` within 1 s).
  - `cargo test -p autumn-stream --tests`, `cargo test -p autumn-partition-server --lib --test-threads=1`, `cargo test -p autumn-manager` ŌĆö green except the pre-existing F116 `register_node_duplicate_addr_rejected` documented flake and the pre-existing F099-I timing-sensitive `cq_flushes_fast_ops_while_slow_op_runs` (passes on single-test rerun).
  - **Live verification (matches user's repro):**
    - `sh cluster.sh reset 4`
    - `./target/release/autumn-client put k1 /tmp/v.txt` ŌåÆ `ok` in ~10 ms.
    - `sh cluster.sh stop-node 1`
    - `./target/release/autumn-client put k2 /tmp/v.txt` ŌåÆ `ok` in **0.22 s** (was `>120 s`).
    - `./target/release/autumn-client info` ŌåÆ log_stream's new tail extent on `[7, 3, 5]` (excludes node 1); within ~10 s the `disk_status_update_loop` flips `node 1 disk online=false` and confirms `node 7 disk online=true`.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) Stop-and-reuse: post-`stop-node 1`, the next `put` returns within `append_fanout_timeout` budget (default 5 s) plus one alloc round-trip.
  - (b) Disk online status reflects reality: dead node's disks flip to `online=false` within one df sweep (10 s); recovered nodes flip back to `online=true` on the next sweep.
  - (c) `select_nodes` skips nodes whose disks are all offline when Ōēź count healthy candidates remain; falls back to all nodes otherwise (preserves pre-F121 fall-back path in `handle_stream_alloc_extent`).
  - (d) New unit test in `crates/rpc/src/client.rs` covers Layer 1.
- **Notes:** Pattern source ŌĆö Go autumn's `streamclient.go:917-941` (any error ŌåÆ 2├Ś retry ŌåÆ `MustAllocNewExtent`) + `pool.go:217-245` (heartbeat-based `IsHealthy`) + `policy.go:16-46` (manager filters allocation candidates by `LastEcho()`). F119 inspires the typed-signal-and-cache-refresh shape (`CODE_EVERSION_MISMATCH` ŌåÆ client `invalidate_extent_cache + retry`); we apply the same shape one layer down for the transport-layer dead-client problem (closed flag ŌåÆ pool evict ŌåÆ fresh connect). Out of scope for this commit: continuous heartbeat in the stream-layer `ConnPool` (Go's `MonitorHealth`) ŌĆö Layer 1+2+3 are sufficient for the symptom; manager-side node-liveness via the heartbeat stream (Go's `LastEcho` ordering) ŌĆö disk-online (df-driven) is the proxy in Layer 5; richer per-disk failure classification ŌĆö extent-node's `mark_disk_offline_for_extent` already handles local-disk faults independently. The disk_id mismatch in the success path is a long-standing pre-F121 bug ŌĆö fixed as part of Layer 4 because mark-on-failure exposed it (the disk would otherwise be permanently stuck offline after one failed first poll).
- **passes:** true

### F129 ┬Ę PutStream / GetStream ŌĆö PS multipart upload + multi-fragment ValuePointer
- **Target:** Bound PS RAM and improve TTFB for large values by adding S3-style multipart upload (`PutBegin` / `PutChunk` / `PutCommit` / `PutAbort`) at the partition server, plus a client-side `GetStream` that loops the existing `GetReq.offset/length`. Memtable / SSTable gain a multi-fragment `ValuePointer` (op flag `OP_VALUE_POINTER_MULTI = 0x40`, encoded `[n_frags:u32][total_len:u64][(extent_id:u64, offset:u32, len:u32) ├Ś n_frags]`); chunks are stored as WAL-shaped records with a new op `OP_CHUNK_BLOB = 0x10` so `decode_records_with_offsets` / `process_gc_chunk` skip them safely. Existing `Put` / `Get` are preserved; both gain a symmetric size cap `AUTUMN_PS_MAX_INLINE_BYTES` (default 64 MiB, hard Ōēż 256 MiB) ŌĆö over-cap requests return `CODE_VALUE_TOO_LARGE`. Client adds a low-level `PutStreamHandle { send, commit, abort }` and high-level `put_stream(Stream<Bytes>)` / `get_stream() -> Stream<Bytes>` / `put_auto` / `get_auto` helpers. PS holds upload sessions in memory only (`HashMap<[u8;16], UploadSession>`); session metadata size is constant in the number of chunks (clients hold the fragment list); idle TTL default 30 min (`AUTUMN_PS_UPLOAD_TTL_SECS`); per-partition session cap default 1024 (`AUTUMN_PS_MAX_UPLOAD_SESSIONS`). PS routing requires `part_id` in `PutChunkReq` / `PutCommitReq` / `PutAbortReq` (`upload_id` alone cannot reach `extract_part_id`).
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) New RPCs `MSG_PUT_BEGIN=0x49` / `MSG_PUT_CHUNK=0x4A` / `MSG_PUT_COMMIT=0x4B` / `MSG_PUT_ABORT=0x4C` round-trip end-to-end.
  - (b) `Put` / `Get` cap is symmetric and rejects over-cap with `CODE_VALUE_TOO_LARGE` before any WAL append or `resolve_value` allocation.
  - (c) Recovery replays `OP_CHUNK_BLOB` records as no-ops; commit records install multi-frag VPs into the recovered memtable.
  - (d) Compaction discard counter fans out per-fragment so every extent containing any live fragment is correctly accounted; v1 GC refuses to punch extents with live multi-frag fragments (documented limit, addressed by F130).
  - (e) `handle_get` / `handle_head` zero-I/O total_len decode for multi-frag VPs.
  - (f) `client.put_auto` routes by size; `client.get_auto` transparently falls back to `get_stream` on `CODE_VALUE_TOO_LARGE`.
  - (g) `autumn-client put-stream --file ... --key ...` + `get-stream --key ... --out ...` round-trip a 1 GiB random file and `cmp` matches.
  - (h) PS RSS during a 1 GiB put-stream stays at chunk-size order of magnitude, not value-size.
- **Evidence:** Design ŌĆö `/Users/zhangdongmao/.claude/plans/resilient-greeting-ember.md`. Touched files (planned): `crates/rpc/src/partition_rpc.rs` (msg_type + 4 Req/Resp + `extract_part_id`), `crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs` (op constants, `PartitionData.upload_sessions`, `decode_records_*` skip, recovery), `crates/partition-server/src/background.rs` (`WriteOp::PutMultiVp`, Phase-1 commit, `resolve_value` multi branch, compaction fan-out, GC v1 µŖæÕłČ), `crates/partition-server/src/rpc_handlers.rs` (`handle_put_begin/chunk/commit/abort`, `handle_get` cap + multi total_len, `handle_head` multi branch, session eviction), `crates/client/src/lib.rs` (handle + helpers), `crates/server/src/bin/autumn_client.rs` (CLI subcommands), `examples/gallery/src/main.rs` (optional: rewrite multipart upload path on top of `put_stream`), README + CLAUDE.md updates, this entry.
- **Notes:** Design rationale ŌĆö picked S3 multipart over autumn-rpc native multi-frame (F133) because it has zero framework impact, matches Azure Blob / GCS / HDFS / GridFS / Ceph industry practice, and dovetails with the existing ValuePointer indirection. Picked multi-fragment VP (╬Č) over a per-upload `blob_stream` (╬Ą) after researching that S3 / Azure Blob / Azure WAS / HDFS / GridFS / Ceph all store large values as fragment lists ŌĆö single-segment continuity gives a measurable advantage only on "client reads whole 1 GiB at once", which is rare in this codebase (gallery already uses 4 MiB Range loops). Client holds the fragment list (not server) so PS state stays O(1) in chunks, sessions don't need persistence, and re-sent chunks after lost ack become harmless orphans cleaned by log_stream truncation. Symmetric `Put` / `Get` cap is critical: an asymmetric cap creates "writable-but-not-readable" footgun. Chunk size hint default = 16 MiB (`AUTUMN_PS_PUT_CHUNK_HINT_BYTES`), enforced range [64 KiB, 64 MiB] server-side. Out of scope (each tracked separately): GC active rewrite (F130), concurrent fragment pread (F131), upload resume across split / PS restart (F132), autumn-rpc native multi-frame (F133), frame-level Put early reject (F134). Test coverage planned: `decode_records_skips_chunk_blob`, `multi_vp_round_trip_encode_decode`, `recovery_installs_multi_vp_entry`, `multi_vp_resolve_subrange_spanning_two_fragments`, `compact_drops_multi_vp_attributes_discards_to_each_extent`, `gc_skips_extent_with_live_multi_vp_fragment`, `handle_get_returns_too_large_above_cap`, `put_returns_too_large_above_cap`, `put_stream_begin_chunk_commit_get_round_trip`, `put_stream_chunk_unknown_upload_id`, `put_auto_routes_big_value_to_stream`, plus E2E `put_stream_recovery` and manual README recipe with a 1 GiB file.
- **passes:** false

### F130 ┬Ę GC active rewrite for multi-fragment VPs (unblocks log_stream extent reclaim under F129)
- **Target:** Implement an "atomic VP rewrite" so log_stream extents holding live multi-frag fragments can be reclaimed. Background task scans sealed log_stream extents whose discard ratio is below the reclaim threshold purely because of live multi-frag VP fragments referencing them; for each such VP, append a fresh contiguous copy of the fragments to the active log_stream extent, then atomically swap the memtable / SSTable VP to point at the new coordinates and bump discard counters on the source extents. Old fragments become discardable; reclaim resumes.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) Concurrent reads against a key being rewritten never return torn / partial values; the read path resolves either the old or the new VP, never a mix.
  - (b) Rewrite serialises correctly with concurrent compact / GC / Put on the same key (well-defined ordering, no double-discard, no lost VP).
  - (c) Workload: long-lived 1 GiB multi-VP value + 24 h of small Puts + periodic GC ŌåÆ log_stream sealed-extent count converges instead of growing unbounded.
  - (d) Per-fragment-VP rewrite throughput bounded by a config knob; rewrite never starves foreground writes.
- **Evidence:** F129 v1 ships GC suppression (`process_gc_chunk` refuses to punch extents with live multi-frag fragments); this entry removes that limit. Touched files (planned): `crates/partition-server/src/background.rs` (rewrite scanner + atomic VP swap), `crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs` (atomic memtable VP swap primitive), tests.
- **Trigger:** v1 monitoring shows log_stream sealed extent count exceeds threshold (candidate: > 16 extents or > 50% sealed extents non-reclaimable), or partition disk usage stays > 80 %.
- **Notes:** Hard problem ŌĆö the linearisation between rewrite, foreground writes, compaction, and GC needs a clean lock / version-stamp story. Likely candidate: piggyback on the existing memtable seq-number to make VP rewrites look like a normal Put with a higher seq, leveraging the existing MVCC machinery rather than introducing a new atomicity primitive. Independent of F129 ŌĆö can ship later in its own PR.
- **passes:** false

### F131 ┬Ę Concurrent fragment pread in `resolve_value` (perf follow-up to F129)
- **Target:** Replace the v1 sequential per-fragment `read_bytes_from_extent` loop in `resolve_value`'s multi-frag branch with `FuturesUnordered`-based concurrent reads, capped at `AUTUMN_PS_RESOLVE_CONCURRENCY` (default 8) to bound per-PS memory and replica fanout.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) 1 GiB / 64-fragment Get end-to-end latency improvement Ōēź 4├Ś over v1 sequential baseline.
  - (b) PS memory under 32 concurrent large-Get load remains bounded (`concurrent_gets ├Ś concurrency_cap ├Ś chunk_size` Ōēż configured RAM).
  - (c) Result Vec is built in fragment order despite out-of-order completion (assemble into pre-allocated `Vec::with_capacity` by per-fragment offset).
- **Evidence:** F129 ships v1 sequential. Touched files (planned): `crates/partition-server/src/background.rs::resolve_value`.
- **Trigger:** Measured 1 GiB `get_auto` / `get_stream` total latency exceeds 60 % of (single-fragment latency ├Ś n_frags), or `examples/gallery` Range read P99 across fragment boundaries materially exceeds intra-fragment P99.
- **Notes:** Cheap PR; one knob, one branch, one test (`multi_vp_resolve_concurrent_completes_in_correct_order`). Independent of F130. Watch for replica thundering-herd on a single hot extent ŌĆö concurrency cap exists for this.
- **passes:** false

### F132 ┬Ę PutStream resume across partition split / PS restart
- **Target:** Persist enough upload-session state so a client whose `PutStreamHandle` was bound to a partition that subsequently split or whose PS rolled can resume from the last committed `chunk_index` instead of re-uploading the whole value. Likely shape: persist `(upload_id, key, must_sync, expires_at, fragments[], total_bytes, last_chunk_index)` as a small region inside `meta_stream`; new owner (post-split / post-restart) loads the region and accepts continuation chunks under the same `upload_id`. New ack-shape on `PutChunkReq` returns a `RESUME_HINT { upload_id, last_committed_index, ps_addr_hint }` when the upload moved to a new PS so the client can reconnect transparently.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) 1 GiB upload at 50 % progress ŌåÆ trigger split ŌåÆ client receives `RESUME_HINT` ŌåÆ continues against the new partition ŌåÆ `commit` succeeds ŌåÆ byte-compare matches.
  - (b) 1 GiB upload at 50 % progress ŌåÆ kill PS ŌåÆ restart ŌåÆ client retries ŌåÆ continues from last committed chunk ŌåÆ `commit` succeeds ŌåÆ byte-compare matches.
  - (c) Per-chunk fsync rate of session-state persistence does not regress small-Put p99 by more than 10 %.
- **Evidence:** F129 v1 client behaviour: split / PS restart mid-upload ŌåÆ caller-level retry from `put_stream_begin`. Touched files (planned): `crates/partition-server/src/lib.rs` (session persistence), `crates/partition-server/src/background.rs` (meta_stream session-region replay), `crates/rpc/src/partition_rpc.rs` (`RESUME_HINT` extension to `PutChunkResp`), `crates/client/src/lib.rs` (handle reconnection).
- **Trigger:** Real workload sees frequent GB-class uploads colliding with split or PS rolls and operators / users complain about wasted bandwidth.
- **Notes:** Hard part is split-time fragment ownership: log_stream CoW makes the chunk bytes visible to both halves of the split, but exactly one half should accept the continued upload. Probably the half whose key range still contains `key`. Persistence cadence: `last_chunk_index` updated lazily (e.g. every K chunks or every T seconds), so a crash loses at most a bounded amount of progress. Worth tackling only after F129 is in production and resume-cost is shown to matter.
- **passes:** false

### F133 ┬Ę autumn-rpc native multi-frame (FLAG_STREAM_END activation)
- **Target:** Activate the reserved `FLAG_STREAM_END = 0x04` frame flag in the autumn-rpc protocol so a single logical RPC can span N request frames and / or N response frames. Extend `RpcClient` with a `call_streaming(req) ŌåÆ impl Stream<Item = Bytes>` entry point, and `handle_*_connection` with a per-`req_id` frame-routing table (`HashMap<u32, mpsc::Sender<Frame>>`) so streaming handlers can pull subsequent frames or push subsequent responses.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) `MSG_RANGE_STREAM` over a 1 M-row range completes with bounded PS memory and end-to-end latency that improves over the chunked-RPC alternative.
  - (b) Existing single-frame RPCs (Put / Get / Head / Range / etc.) behave identically ŌĆö no regression for non-streaming handlers, no per-frame overhead for the common case.
  - (c) Cancellation: dropping the client `Stream` aborts the server handler within bounded time.
- **Evidence:** Frame format already reserves `FLAG_STREAM_END` (`crates/rpc/src/frame.rs`) ŌĆö defined and parsed but never set or checked. PutStream / GetStream (F129) deliberately did **not** use this ŌĆö multipart was simpler and matches industry practice. Touched files (planned): `crates/rpc/src/frame.rs`, `crates/rpc/src/client.rs`, `crates/rpc/src/server.rs`, every `handle_*_connection` site.
- **Trigger:** Decoupled from F129. Real triggers: (1) `MSG_RANGE` returning > 100 k rows hits the single-frame size limit or pushes PS memory unacceptably high, or (2) autumn-rs adds a watch / subscribe RPC whose semantics inherently require server streaming.
- **Notes:** Multipart (F129) is preferred for "one big payload" flows because it gives idempotent commit, S3-shape resume (F132), and zero framework impact. Native streaming wins specifically for "many small results from one logical query" (range scans) or "open-ended subscription" (watch). Wire compat: the flag bit is currently unused by all senders; activating it on a per-RPC basis preserves existing behaviour. Out of scope: re-implementing PutStream / GetStream on top of native multi-frame (the multipart shape already wins on resumability).
- **passes:** false

### F134 ┬Ę Frame-level Put early reject (perf hardening for F129 cap)
- **Target:** Move the `AUTUMN_PS_MAX_INLINE_BYTES` cap check from the post-rkyv-decode path (F129 v1) into the autumn-rpc frame loop: when `payload_len > cap + overhead_bound`, reject the frame and either close the connection or return `CODE_VALUE_TOO_LARGE` without reading the body bytes off the socket.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) A client that sends a 1 GiB `MSG_PUT` body never causes the PS to allocate a 1 GiB `Bytes` ŌĆö the connection is dropped or the request is rejected after only the frame header is read.
  - (b) Legitimate borderline requests (just under cap) still succeed.
  - (c) No regression to small-Put p99.
- **Evidence:** F129 ships rkyv-decode-then-check; that costs one network transfer per rejected request. Touched files (planned): `crates/rpc/src/frame.rs` / per-service frame-loop hooks; `extract_part_id`-style schema metadata for "where in the payload is the value field" so the check can be done from header alone.
- **Trigger:** Monitoring shows PS network ingress carries a non-trivial rate (> 1 %) of `CODE_VALUE_TOO_LARGE` rejections, indicating clients are not using `put_auto` correctly and the wasted transfer is material.
- **Notes:** Tricky bit: cap applies to "value bytes inside the payload", not "raw payload bytes" ŌĆö rkyv adds a small constant overhead, so the bound has to be `cap + overhead_bound`. Easier alternative: cap raw `payload_len` directly with a slightly higher number (`cap + 64 KiB`); rejection is proxied through the same `CODE_VALUE_TOO_LARGE` shape. Independent of F133.
- **passes:** false

### F116 ┬Ę gallery `/get/` slow + autumn-extent CPU after EC conversion (stale `extent_info_cache`, no eversion check on read)
- **Target:** After `ec_conversion_dispatch_loop` flips a sealed extent from 3-replica to EC (e.g. 3+1), `StreamClient.extent_info_cache` (`crates/stream/src/client.rs:619`) still holds the pre-EC `ExtentInfo` (`replicates`, `parity=[]`, old `eversion`). The PS reads against three stale-replica addresses whose `.dat` has been truncated to one shard's worth (`write_shard_local`, `extent_node.rs:2037-2065`), burning up to `3 ├Ś 3 s` (`pool.call_timeout`, `client.rs:1568`) on `read_replicated_with_failover` (`client.rs:1497-1518`) before the cache is finally evicted on error. Compounded by two server-side gaps: client passes `eversion: 0` (`client.rs:1562`) which disables the existing eversion guard at `extent_node.rs:2219`, and `write_shard_local` never bumps `entry.eversion` so the local view would still match pre-EC even if the client did pass a real value. User-visible symptom: `curl http://0.0.0.0:5001/get/<KEY>` takes multiple seconds on the first attempt after conversion and `autumn-extent` shows elevated CPU (mostly EC-encode for in-progress extents + read amplification). Make the read path self-heal on stale-cache without manager push.
- **Evidence:** `crates/manager/src/recovery.rs:531-568` (`apply_ec_conversion_done` writes new layout + `eversion += 1` to the manager's etcd / in-memory store with no client notification). `crates/stream/src/client.rs:1397-1417` (`fetch_extent_info` is cache-only on hit; never proactively refreshed; `invalidate_extent_cache` at `:1421-1423` only called by tests). `crates/stream/src/extent_node.rs:2219-2227` (server eversion guard returns `FailedPrecondition` Err when `req.eversion > 0 && req.eversion < ev` ŌĆö but client passes 0, so the check is dead code on the read path). `crates/stream/src/extent_node.rs:2037-2065` (`write_shard_local` updates `len`/`sealed_length`/`avali` but not `eversion`). The user observed the slow GET on a live cluster where `autumn-client info` correctly shows EC layout because `info` bypasses the cache and fetches directly from the manager (`autumn_client.rs:2164-2237`).
- **Fix:**
  1. Plumb a `new_eversion = ex.eversion + 1` from the manager's `ec_conversion_dispatch_loop` through `ExtConvertToEcReq` (`crates/rpc/src/manager_rpc.rs`) ŌåÆ `ConvertToEcReq` (`crates/stream/src/extent_rpc.rs`) ŌåÆ `WriteShardReq` (binary header 20 ŌåÆ 28 bytes, eversion is the 4th u64 after `extent_id`/`shard_index`/`sealed_length`).
  2. `write_shard_local` writes `entry.eversion = new_eversion` and persists via `save_meta`. `apply_ec_conversion_done` *assigns* the same `new_eversion` (was `+= 1` ad-hoc) so manager + every shard host agree on the post-EC eversion at conversion completion.
  3. Add `CODE_EVERSION_MISMATCH = 6` to `extent_rpc.rs`. `handle_read_bytes` returns it (instead of an Err `FailedPrecondition`) when the client's eversion is stale.
  4. `read_shard_from_addr` accepts an `eversion` parameter (caller passes `ex.eversion`). On `CODE_EVERSION_MISMATCH` it returns a private `EversionStale` anyhow sentinel.
  5. `read_bytes_from_extent` runs a 2-attempt loop: on `EversionStale` from the inner `read_with_layout` it calls `invalidate_extent_cache(extent_id)` and refetches `ExtentInfo` once. `read_replicated_with_failover` and the EC paths (`ec_subrange_read`, `ec_read_full`) fail-fast on `EversionStale` rather than walking the remaining stale replicas (every replica reports the same mismatch by construction).
- **Verification:**
  - cargo build --workspace: clean (only pre-existing dead-code warnings).
  - cargo test -p autumn-stream --tests --test-threads=1: 70/70 pass (one test, `cq_flushes_fast_ops_while_slow_op_runs`, is timing-sensitive and only stable serially ŌĆö pre-existing).
  - cargo test -p autumn-manager --lib: 1 pre-existing failure (`register_node_duplicate_addr_rejected` ŌĆö confirmed via `git stash` to be unrelated).
  - autumn-manager full integration tests: deferred (live etcd + manager-server already running on 127.0.0.1:2379 / :9001 in the user's environment).
  - **Live cluster verification (deferred to operator):** pick an EC-converted extent (`autumn-client info` shows `EC(K+M), data=[ŌĆ”], parity=[ŌĆ”]`); `time curl -o /dev/null http://0.0.0.0:5001/get/<KEY>`. Pre-fix: > 3 s on first GET, fast on second. Post-fix: fast on the first GET (one extra manager `extent_info` RTT, then steady-state cached EC reads). `top -pid $(pgrep autumn-extent | head -1)` over a 50-GET loop should stay flat (no per-request 3-replica fanout amplification); residual encode CPU during active conversion is expected. Confirm `xxd -s 24 -l 8 ŌĆ”meta` on each shard host matches the manager's view of `eversion`.
- **Acceptance:**
  - (a) Ō£ō Wire format change: `WriteShardReq` 20 ŌåÆ 28 bytes, `ConvertToEcReq`/`ExtConvertToEcReq` carry eversion. No backward compat needed (single-tenant cluster, all binaries rebuilt together).
  - (b) Ō£ō Client passes real eversion in `ReadBytesReq`; server returns `CODE_EVERSION_MISMATCH` on stale; client refetches once.
  - (c) Ō£ō Coordinator + every WriteShard target bump local `entry.eversion` and persist via `save_meta`.
  - (d) ŌÜĀ Live cluster GET-latency / CPU verification deferred to operator restart.
- **Notes:** Implemented + tested + documented (`crates/stream/CLAUDE.md` Programming Note 14). The stale-cache window is the only known correctness/perf gap that EC conversion left behind; resolved in-band with no new RPCs and no manager push (matches the codebase's existing pull-on-mismatch idiom ŌĆö `extent_node.rs:2802` "no etcd watch in Rust implementation"). Performance impact: server-side ReadBytes adds one u64 comparison after the existing atomic load (~1 ns); client-side adds one branch on `resp.code` before `CODE_OK` (~1 ns); the retry loop runs once in the happy path. Out of scope: reducing peak CPU during bulk EC conversion (Reed-Solomon encode of multi-GiB extents is intrinsically expensive ŌĆö if it ever becomes a problem, throttle `ec_conversion_dispatch_loop` to one extent at a time or move encode to a dedicated thread).
- **passes:** true

### F117 ┬Ę EC encode/decode/reconstruct must run on a dedicated OS thread, not the compio event loop
- **Target:** Stop the Reed-Solomon encode/decode/reconstruct calls from blocking the compio event loop. User-observed symptom: during `ec_conversion_dispatch_loop`-driven EC conversion, `autumn-extent` becomes sluggish on append/read RPCs even though no I/O is contended ŌĆö the event loop is monopolised by `crate::erasure::ec_encode` running synchronously inside `handle_convert_to_ec`. Same hazard exists on (b) `run_ec_recovery_payload` (RS reconstruct of a missing shard) and (c) `StreamClient::ec_read_full` (RS decode of k+m shards on a fallback / full-extent read), each of which can block its host runtime for 100ŌĆō300 ms on a 128 MiB extent.
